activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(5).)
PUBLIC COMMENT
During the public comment period, members of the public may speak on general items of interest within the Commission's
jurisdiction that are not on the agenda.  Each member of the public may speak for a maximum of three minutes with a maximum of
15 minutes for the entire public comment period. The Chair shall determine whether the matter is within the Commission's
jurisdiction. The Commission shall not act on or discuss any matters raised during the public comment period, which are not on the
agenda, but shall refer such matters to staff for review and/or request such matters be placed on a future agenda.

Account Number:

TO:
Planning Commission
FROM:
Zachary Dahl, Interim Director
PREPARED BY:
Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
July 25, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Pre-Application Review for a Proposed Office and Residential Mixed-Use Development at 668 E. 3rd Ave. and 316 S. 
Eldorado St. (Post + Beam)
RECOMMENDATION:
Review the proposed project on a preliminary basis, receive public comments, and provide input to the applicant and staff 
pertaining to the following project elements:
1.
Proposed Uses – Compatibility of the proposed office and residential uses with the adjacent neighborhood, and 
consideration of other neighborhood commercial or support service uses onsite;
2.
Building Design – Architectural design, building height and massing, and transition with surrounding buildings;
3.
Site Plan and Landscape – Proposed pedestrian realm improvements and transition to the Downtown Retail Core; 
and,
4.
Other project aspects that should be considered during the formal planning application.
BACKGROUND:
Gateway Crossing SM, LLC (Applicant) has submitted the subject Pre-Application, PA-2023-025 (Project) to demolish all 
existing structures on the two parcels bound by E. 3rd Avenue, S. Delaware Street, and S. Eldorado Street, and construct a 
new mixed-use development called “Post + Beam,” consisting of a seven-story residential building and a six-story office 
building with two levels of underground parking. As proposed, the project will require a Site Plan and Architectural Review 
(SPAR) and Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) for construction of the new mixed-use buildings, tree removal, 
and grading.
The applicant held a formal pre-application neighborhood meeting on June 26, 2023, in which approximately 20 members 
of the public attended. Discussion generally focused on recommendations on building and site design improvements, 
consideration of other neighborhood commercial uses, lack of sufficient onsite parking, and general concerns for 
downtown development and congestion. Further discussion is provided within the Items for Planning Commission 
Discussion section of this report. 
For this Study Session, the Planning Commission should focus its review on the project’s proposed land uses, building and 
site design, and other aspects necessary for the Commission to make positive findings and recommend approval of the 
project when the application returns for a formal public hearing. Additionally, staff requests that the Commission provide 
input and direction on other project and design aspects, if any, that should be considered during the formal planning 
application.

--- page 12 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
PROJECT DESCRIPTION:
Project Site
The project site consists of two contiguous parcels located on the partial block bound by E. 3rd Avenue, S. Delaware Street, 
S. Eldorado Street, and a gas station. The combined parcel area is approximately 0.98 acres, or 42,643 square feet. The site 
is designated Downtown Retail Core Support in the City’s General Plan Land Use Plan and is zoned CBD/S (Central Business 
District Support). The existing on-site uses include a three-story commercial/medical office building that was built in 1989, 
and a one-story commercial shopping plaza that was originally constructed in 1978. The City’s historic review consultant 
prepared a historic evaluation of the existing commercial shopping plaza structure as it is 45 years old and determined that 
it does not qualify as a historic resource. The project is located outside the Downtown Historic District, which is located 
approximately two and a half blocks west of the project site. 
Adjacent uses include a variety of commercial and residential uses as follows:
•
North: Gas station (Shell) and a two-story commercial building with beauty salon, retail and restaurant uses.
•
South: Gas station (Gas & Stop) and Block 21 Mixed-Use Project, which is approved for office and residential uses 
(site demolished, pending building permit issuance).
•
East: Four-story multi-family residential building zoned R5-D (the Metropolitan).
•
West: Auto-repair facility (Jiffy Lube) and a two-story commercial building with retail and restaurant uses.
The Downtown Caltrain Station is located approximately 0.4-miles to the west of the project site. A location map showing 
the project site, its vicinity, and adjacent zoning designations is included as Attachment 1.
Proposed Project, Building Program, and Site Plan
The proposed “Post + Beam” project is an office and residential mixed-use development with a combined floor area of 
approximately 192,000 square feet resulting in a floor area ratio (FAR) of 4.5. The office building is located on the west 
parcel is approximately 132,000 square feet in size with a height of 88 feet (six stories) and two levels of underground 
parking (239 spaces). The residential building on the east parcel has a height of 84 feet (seven stories) and includes 59 
units with garage parking at the ground level (eight spaces). The proposed residential unit mix includes 18 studio units, 24 
one-bedroom units, and 17 two-bedroom units, all of which would be rental apartments. Of the 59 units, seven units (14 
percent of the base density) are proposed as below market rate (BMR) at the Low-income category, and the applicant 
proposes to pay a Fractional Unit Fee for the remaining 1 percent (0.35 units), pursuant to the City’s inclusionary 
requirements.
The office lobby entrance is located midblock on E. 3rd Avenue and the residential lobby entrance is along S. Eldorado 
Street. The S. Eldorado Street frontage also provides access to both garage driveways and rooms dedicated to trash and 
mechanical equipment for each building. The office building has two levels of below-grade parking that provides up to 239 
off-street parking stalls through a proposed mechanical vehicle stacking system. A detailed operations plan for the 
mechanical parking system is required upon formal application submittal. The residential building has a parking garage 
with eight parking spaces at the ground level. The applicant has indicated that additional residential parking may be 
provided through a private, shared parking agreement with the adjacent Metropolitan apartment building. The project 
also proposes to widen sidewalks along the office building frontages on E. Delaware Street, E. 3rd Avenue and S. Eldorado 
Street to provide approximately 4,393 square-feet of at-grade open space for the public. Open spaces for residential uses 
include private unit balconies and approximately 2,540 square feet of shared open space. The project proposes new street 
trees along all frontages except for S. Delaware Street. In accordance with the City’s Street Tree Master Plan and Municipal 
Code, street trees are required along all frontages of the project site.
A contemporary architectural style is proposed for both office and residential buildings. The design utilizes a variety of 
exterior wall materials and textures to break the massing into smaller elements, which is an approach seen with nearby 
mixed-use projects. A discussion of the building design is provided in the Items for Planning Commission Discussion section 
below. Project plans showing the proposed site plan, floor plans, and building elevations are included in Attachment 2.

--- page 13 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
APPLICABLE CODE AND POLICY REVIEW:
General Plan
The General Plan Land Use Map designates the project site as Downtown Retail Core Support, which is meant to provide 
uses at intensities that complement both the downtown core and the adjacent residential neighborhoods. A preliminary 
list of General Plan policies applicable to the proposed project is included in Attachment 3.
As a mixed-use project, it would be consistent with Land Use Element policy LU 1.8 Mixed Use Commercial-Residential, 
which promotes housing production in non-residential zones. The project would also be consistent with Land Use Element 
policy LU 3.1 Downtown Plan, as a large office and high-density residential project located within downtown. Additional 
discussion on the project’s consistency with certain General Plan policies is included in the Items for Planning Commission 
Discussion section of this report.
Zoning Code
The project site is zoned CBD/S (Central Business District Support), which implements the goals of the General Plan in 
encouraging commercial uses that support the downtown core to the west and serve adjacent residential neighborhoods. 
The CBD/S zone is also subject to development standards in Chapter 27.39 of the Municipal Code, including floor area, 
residential density, setbacks, open space, loading and bicycle parking. The project site is also within the limits of the 
Central Parking Improvement District (CPID), which functions as the downtown’s parking district. It should be noted that 
Assembly Bill 2097 precludes the City from imposing off-street parking requirements on projects within one-half mile of a 
major public transit stop. Therefore, the project is not required to provide any vehicle parking or pay in-lieu fees since it is 
located 0.4-miles from the Downtown Caltrain Station.
A project data sheet listing the applicable Zoning Code standards are included in Attachment 4. As currently proposed, the 
project exceeds the maximum building height (55 feet), residential density (50 units/acre), floor area ratio limits (3.0), and 
does not show all required residential open space, bicycle parking and loading facilities. However, the applicant intends to 
request concessions and waivers from specific development standards pursuant to State Density Bonus Law. A discussion 
of the project’s density bonus requests is provided in the State Density Bonus Law section below. 
Downtown Area Plan – Gateway Sub-Area
The project site is located within the City’s Downtown Area Plan. The Downtown Plan establishes goals and policies to 
implement the overall vision of the downtown area. Applicable goals that pertain to the project include:
•
Enhance Downtown’s Role as the City Center and Maintain Its Unique Sense of Place
•
Enhance the Vitality and Activity of Downtown by Incorporating an Overall Good Mix and Diversity of Uses
•
Enhance the Downtown’s Pedestrian Environment and Enhance the Safety and Attractiveness of Downtown
The project site is also within the Gateway sub-area in the Downtown Plan and is subject to the Vision of the Gateway 
design guidelines, which encourages enhanced visual and pedestrian connections to link the Gateway and the Downtown 
Retail Core. Recommended improvements include street trees, streetlights, building setbacks, and additional building step 
backs on the residential building’s upper floors along S. Eldorado Street. Additional discussion on the project’s consistency 
with certain Downtown Plan policies is included in the Items for Planning Commission Discussion section of this report.
State Density Bonus Law and Local Inclusionary Requirements
California Government Code Section 65915 outlines density bonus standards for residential and mixed-use projects that 
designate a portion of residential units as affordable, or below market rate (BMR). The City also has an adopted BMR 
Inclusionary Program that requires residential developments to designate at least 15 percent of their base density units as 
affordable at the Low-Income or Very Low-Income level for rental projects, or 15 percent of units at the Low-Income or 
Moderate-income level for ownership projects. For reference, a Very Low-Income unit is affordable for families or 
individuals who make up to 50% of Area Median Income (AMI), Low-Income is affordable up to 80% of AMI and Moderate 
is affordable up to 120% of AMI. For 2023, the AMI in San Mateo County for an individual is $122,500 and a family of four 
is $175,000. 
The project’s zoning designation of CBD/S permits a maximum base density of 50 units per acre, which yields the 0.98-acre

--- page 14 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
site with a base density of 49 units. The applicant proposes to satisfy the City’s 15 percent inclusionary requirement by 
devoting 14 percent of the base 49 units as affordable at the Low-Income level, which equates to seven BMR units, and 
paying a Fractional Unit Fee for the remaining 1 percent (0.35 units). This entitles the project to a density bonus of up to 
26 percent, resulting in a maximum allowable density of 62 units. As designed, the project proposes a total of 59 units, 
which is within the maximum allowable density and inclusive of the density bonus.
Concession and Waiver Requests 
Designating 14 percent of the units as affordable at the Low-Income level makes the project eligible for one concession 
and additional waivers. At this time, the applicant has requested one concession and three waivers as outlined in the 
project’s preliminary density bonus request letter (Attachment 5). The concession requested is to increase the maximum 
building height from 55 feet to 88 feet for the office building.
In accordance with Government Code Section 65915(d)(1), the City shall grant the concession request unless findings can 
be made that the concession would: 1) not result in identifiable and actual cost reductions to provide the affordable 
housing units, 2) have a specific adverse impact upon public health and safety, or 3) be contrary to state or federal law.
In addition to the concession request, the project is seeking three waivers:
1.
Increase the maximum Floor Area Ratio from 3.0 to 4.5;
2.
Increase the maximum building height from 55 feet to 84 feet for the residential building; and,
3.
Reduce the residential common open space requirement from a minimum of 7,080 square feet to 2,540 square 
feet.
State Density Bonus Law provides that waivers are reductions from standards that would otherwise physically preclude the 
development of the project at the proposed density. The City shall grant the waiver requests unless findings can be made 
that granting the waiver would have an adverse impact on any historical resource or would be contrary to state or federal 
law. The waiver and concession requests are considered preliminary at this stage and may be modified during the formal 
planning application stage. Staff will conduct a full evaluation of all waiver and concession requests during the formal 
planning application review.
Pedestrian Master Plan
The City’s Pedestrian Master Plan contains recommendations to improve the pedestrian realm throughout the City. 
Appendix A of the Pedestrian Master Plan provides guidelines for sidewalk designs and types specific to a project’s land 
use and street parking configuration. Along the project’s office building frontages on E. 3rd Avenue and S. Delaware Street, 
the applicable sidewalk standard is A.9 Mixed Use Type A Zero Setbacks. This standard recommends an overall sidewalk 
width ranging from 16 feet to 20 feet. Along the project frontage on S. Eldorado Street, the applicable sidewalk standard is 
A.10 Mixed Use Type B Street Parking, which recommends an overall sidewalk width ranging from 16 feet to 26 feet. It 
should also be noted that the Municipal Code requires that new developments in the CBD/S zone be built to the property 
line unless building setbacks are provided for the provision of open space or landscaping. Additionally, the project is 
located within the Downtown Area Plan, Gateway Sub-area, which requires a minimum 15-foot setback for the residential 
building along S. Eldorado Street.
Based on staff’s review of the preliminary project plans, the site plan is not consistent with the Pedestrian Master Plan for 
overall sidewalk and zone widths, with the exception of S. Eldorado Street. Prior to or during the formal planning 
application stage, staff will request additional information in the project plans to conduct a more detailed evaluation of 
the sidewalk designs, including for wider overall sidewalk widths to achieve greater consistency with the Pedestrian 
Master Plan.
Bicycle Master Plan
The City’s Bicycle Master Plan provides policies and recommendations to implement citywide infrastructure improvements 
to support bicycle use. The Bicycle Master Plan also lays out a proposed bicycle network of various bicycle lanes, paths, 
and routes. Specific to this project site, the Bicycle Master Plan calls for a separated bicycle lane (Class IV) along the 
project’s E. 3rd Avenue and S. Delaware Street frontages. A full evaluation of the project’s consistency with the Bicycle

--- page 15 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Master Plan will be completed during the formal planning application phase.
ITEMS FOR PLANNING COMMISSION DISCUSSION:
Proposed Uses
As discussed above, the applicant proposes a mixed-use building with office and residential uses, which are permitted uses 
in the CBD/S District. In accordance with Municipal Code Section 27.39.020, the CBD/S District also permits other 
commercial uses, including restaurants, retail, personal services, schools, and daycare facilities. It should be noted that 
residential uses in this zone are permitted only as part of mixed-use development. While this project would satisfy this 
requirement, the project proposes the same combination of uses (office and residential) as other nearby mixed-use 
developments that have been recently approved or constructed. While retail and other neighborhood commercial uses are 
not required uses in this zone, the Downtown Area Plan establishes goals that encourage provision of commercial uses in 
the Gateway sub-area that support surrounding residents, employees, and visitors. The General Plan also contains Land 
Use policies (LU 2.4, 2.8, and 2.9) that encourage convenience retail and support service uses adjacent to residential 
neighborhoods. These uses are intended to serve as a transition between the Gateway residential areas to the commercial 
downtown core.
At the project’s neighborhood meeting, members of the public raised concerns that this project, along with other recent 
mixed-use projects in the downtown area, have resulted in the loss of neighborhood commercial uses, such as small-scale 
retail, a grocery store, and local restaurants. Members of the public also expressed concerns that too much new office 
space is being built in the downtown area. At this time, staff is seeking Planning Commission input on the project’s 
proposed land uses (office and residential), and if other uses should be considered. When evaluating the proposed land 
use mix, staff recommends the Planning Commission use City adopted plans and policies to support their 
recommendations and consider the following questions:
1.
What neighborhood serving commercial or support service uses should be incorporated into the project? These 
uses could include, but are not limited to, retail, restaurants, schools, day care facilities, and markets that can 
serve adjacent residential neighborhoods and commercial uses.
2.
If these uses should be incorporated, along what frontage(s) should the applicant consider incorporating these 
uses?
Building Design
The project is designed in a Contemporary Style due to the amount of glass and other exterior materials that inform the 
overall building form. The office building is composed of cement plaster at the ground floor and upper two floors. The 
second through fourth floors of the office building includes corrugated metal walls panels painted in a deep red or gray 
color. A simulated wood material is proposed for the overhangs above the office lobby entrance and sixth floor terrace to 
provide additional variation and interest to the office building. The residential building utilizes a different material palette 
that is primarily brick veneer and cement plaster in neutral colors. Horizontal wood siding is also proposed for portions of 
the residential building that is slightly stepped back or recessed. The design incorporates variation in exterior wall 
materials and textures, and subtle changes in colors and materials as attempts to break up the building mass horizontally 
and vertically. Since the project is located on the eastern edge of downtown, staff recommended further consideration 
and improvements to the project’s transition with the lower scale buildings and residential zones directly north and east of 
the project site. During the initial project review, staff identified opportunities to improve the project design by providing 
stronger building corner treatments, improving pedestrian scale elements and treatment to the building base, and 
increasing variation in window treatments. These comments are included within the pre-application review letter as 
Attachment 6.
The surrounding neighborhood consists of mixed-use office, residential and commercial uses that vary in scale and height. 
Block 21, a six-story, mixed-use office and residential development, is located across the project site on S. Delaware Street. 
A four-story multi-family apartment complex, the Metropolitan, is across the project on S. Eldorado Street. There are 
several lower scale buildings located directly north and south of the site that include one to two-story commercial 
buildings. The project proposes two buildings at six and seven stories in height, which exceeds the height of adjacent 
buildings by one to six stories. In accordance with the Gateway design guidelines, the project should provide additional

--- page 16 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
step backs for the upper floors (above 25 feet) of the residential building. This will also improve the transition with the 
adjacent multifamily building across the project site on S. Eldorado Street. 
Staff has also received public comments that the project should consider a traditional architectural style that is less “boxy,” 
“monolithic,” and relates to the historic architectural character of Downtown. In addition, the City’s Objective Design 
Standards (ODS) for Multi-Family Projects is anticipated for adoption by the end of the year, which would likely take effect 
during the formal planning application review of the residential building. 
To guide revisions of the project’s design before the formal application submittal, staff is seeking the Planning 
Commission’s input on the overall style, massing, and transition to adjacent buildings, as well as identification of other 
design revisions that could improve the overall project and how it fits into the larger Downtown context. When evaluating 
the proposed building design, staff recommends the Planning Commission consider the following questions:
1.
Is the proposed Contemporary architectural style appropriate for this neighborhood? Should a different 
architectural style be considered? 
2.
What design treatments and/or modifications should the applicant consider to improve the overall building height, 
mass and scale, and its relationship to the surrounding context? This could include, but is not limited to, changes in 
building height, stepbacks and/or massing.
Site and Landscape Plan
The Vision of the Gateway sets forth design goals to enhance the Gateway as a prominent entry feature to the City and 
Downtown core through various site plan and landscape treatments. The document contains additional setback 
requirements to ensure a consistent building rhythm and enhanced pedestrian environment for new residential 
development. Currently, the proposed residential building does not meet the Gateway Vision design guidelines for the S. 
Eldorado Street frontage, which requires a minimum building setback of 15 feet to 20 feet. The additional setbacks would 
improve the transition with adjacent residential buildings (Metropolitan) and bring the project into greater conformance 
with the Pedestrian Master Plan for recommended sidewalk widths along S. Eldorado Street.
In addition to the Gateway design guidelines, the City’s Zoning Code requires street tree plantings, usable open space, and 
overall site landscaping to compliment new mixed-use developments in the Downtown area. The residential building is 
required to provide open space through a combination of private and common (shared) open space area that is subject to 
the Zoning Code’s usable open space standards. Although the project proposes private balconies, none are creditable as 
they do not meet the minimum dimensions. As proposed, the project provides approximately 2,540 square feet of 
creditable common open space, which is less than the required 7,080 square feet for a residential building of this size. As 
noted above, the applicant intends to request a State Density Bonus waiver to reduce overall open space requirements for 
the residential building.
Currently, the project proposes to widen sidewalks and provide street furnishing and enhanced landscaping along the 
office building frontages on S. Delaware Street, E. 3rd Avenue and S. Eldorado Street. These improvements provide 
approximately 3,114 square feet of at-grade open space, which meets the minimum at-grade open space requirements for 
the office component of the project. 
At this time, staff is seeking Planning Commission input on the proposed site plan and landscape improvements and its 
overall consistency in meeting the Gateway goals.
1.
What site plan and/or landscape treatments should the applicant consider to further improve the pedestrian 
realm?
2.
Does the proposed project accomplish the Gateway design goals to enhance the connection to the Downtown 
Retail Core? What additional improvements should be considered?
PUBLIC COMMENTS:
As discussed previously, the applicant held a formal pre-application neighborhood meeting on June 26, 2023. The 
applicant’s summary of the neighborhood meeting is included in Attachment 7. Public comments submitted to City staff

--- page 17 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
during the pre-application review are included in Attachment 8. A total of eleven public comments were submitted and 
generally raise concerns about lack of sufficient onsite parking, overall downtown development and traffic congestion, 
request consideration of other uses instead of office, and recommend design modifications that include support for more 
traditional or Contemporary Mediterranean architectural styles. A letter citing the Housing Accountability Act (HAA) was 
provided; however, HAA is not applicable because the project currently proposes less than two-thirds of the mixed-use 
buildings’ floor area for residential uses. Any public comments received after publication of this report will be forwarded to 
the Planning Commission for consideration at the study session and posted to this item on the City’s Agendas & Minutes 
Public Meeting Portal as “Post Packet Public Comments.”
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
In accordance with Public Resources Code Section 21065, the review of a pre-application is not a project under the 
California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) because the Planning Commission is not taking any action at this time. An 
environmental review will be conducted as part of the formal planning application in conformance with CEQA.
NEXT STEPS:
Following this Study Session, the applicant will have an opportunity to revise the project based on the comments and input 
provided by staff, the public, and the Planning Commission. As currently proposed, the project is anticipated to require the 
following planning applications, which would be subject to recommendation by the Planning Commission and final action 
by the City Council in accordance with Municipal Code Section 27.06.050(d):
1.
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) for the construction of mixed-use buildings consisting of office uses and 
59 residential units; and,
2.
Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) for the removal of trees greater than six inches in diameter.
Sample Findings of Approval for the above planning application types are included in Attachment 9.

THIS SET OF DRAWINGS IS FOR A NEW 6-STORY + BASEMENT MASS TIMBER OFFICE BUILDING OF APPROXIMATELY 127,956 SF 
AT THE INTERSECTION OF S. DELAWARE STREET AND 3RD AVENUE IN SAN MATEO, CA. THIS PROJECT INCLUDES ON- AND 
OFF-SITE IMPROVEMENTS INCLUDING GROUND-LEVEL AND TERRACE LANDSCAPING AND PUBLIC RIGHT-OF-WAY 
IMPROVEMENTS.
NEW BUILDING CONSTRUCTION WILL STRIVE TO MEET USGBC LEED GOLD STANDARDS, AND WILL BE IN FULL COMPLIANCE 
WITH CALIFORNIA GREEN BUILDING CODE. THE BUILDING IS ALSO EXPECTED TO RUN ON ALL-ELECTRIC SYSTEMS.

LOOKING SOUTHWEST ON 3RD AVE., TREE CANOPY CONTINUES FROM RESIDENTIAL ACROSS THE STREET,
AND 3 ACCENT TREES FRAME THE MID-BLOCK ENTRANCE. BULBOUT AND CURB EXTENSION ALLOW FOR
ENHANCED PLANTING AND STORMWATER TREATMENT.
LOOKING NORTH DOWN EL DORADO ST. AT LOADING ZONE AND GARAGE ENTRY.
BULBOUTAT INTERSECTION ALLOWS FOR ENHANCED PLANTING AREA.
LOADING ZONE ENTRY AT EL DORADO, RAISED PLANTERS AND SEATING AREA. BULBOUT AT INTERSECTION
ALLOWS FOR  ENHANCED  PLANTING AREA.

ATTACHMENT 3
GENERAL PLAN ELEMENTS AND POLICIES
PA-2023-025, 668 E. 3RD AVE., POST + BEAM PRE-APPLICATION
600-680 E. 3RD AVE. AND 316 S. ELDORADO ST.
SAN MATEO, CA 94401
PARCEL # 034-188-140 and -150
City of San Mateo – Applicable Policies
Development of the site is guided by the following relevant planning documents:
1. General Plan Vision 2030 (Adopted October 18, 2010)
Available online at:  https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/1537/General-Plan
2. City of San Mateo Zoning Code
Available online at:  https://law.cityofsanmateo.org/us/ca/cities/san-mateo/code/27
3. City of San Mateo Downtown Area Plan and Vision of the Gateway
Available online at: 
https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/DocumentCenter/View/55327/2009-Downtown-Area-
Plan
https://cityofsanmateo.org/DocumentCenter/View/69321/Vision-of-the-Gateway
4. Bicycle Master Plan (April 2020)
Available online at: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/DocumentCenter/View/85445 
5. Pedestrian Master Plan (April 2012)
Available online at: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/2218/Pedestrian-Master-Plan 
Applicable General Plan Elements and Policies are listed to facilitate further discussion and 
direction for the project at this preliminary stage.  The formal planning application submittal will 
be required to provide further clarification and/or documentation to ensure conformance with 
all applicable polices and guidelines.    
Land Use Element
LU 1.5: 
Building Height. Maintain maximum building height limits contained in Appendix 
C, and as specified in Policy LU 6A.2, closely matched with the Land Use 
categories and Building Intensity standards.
LU 1.8: 
Mixed Use Commercial-Residential. Facilitate housing production by allowing 
commercial mixed-use development which includes multi-family dwellings in all 
non-residential land use categories except service commercial, 
manufacturing/industrial, and parks/open space.

--- page 78 ---
General Plan Elements and Policies
PA-2023-025, 668 E. 3rd Ave., Post + Beam Pre-Application
Page 2 of 8
LU 1.10:
Commercial Development. Encourage industrial, service, retail, and office 
development which is compatible with the desired character of the area and with 
adjacent residential areas in terms of intensity of use, height, bulk and design as 
delineated on the Land Use Plan, Building Height Plan and Building Intensity Plan. 
Commercial development adjacent to residential areas shall address concerns 
pertaining to traffic, truck loading, trash/recycling activities, noise, visual impacts, 
and public safety including hazardous material storage, fire safety, air pollutant 
emissions and odors.
LU 2.3: 
Local Employment. Encourage uses, which provide opportunities for employment 
of all the City's residents, with emphasis placed on major employers that provide 
high value-added jobs.
LU 2.4          Downtown Plan. Establish downtown San Mateo as the social, cultural, and 
economic center of the City with a wide range of office, medical, residential, 
entertainment, and retail uses at high intensities and densities while encourage 
pedestrian activity and bicycle connectivity to adjacent neighborhoods.
LU 2.8: 
Convenience Retail. Encourage and preserve convenience retail uses located 
adjacent to residential neighborhoods.
LU 3.1:
Downtown Plan. As the social, cultural and economic center of the City, the 
downtown shall maintain a wide range of office, medical, residential, 
entertainment, and retail uses at high intensities and densities.
LU 4.2: 
Developer's Contribution Policy. Require new development to pay on an 
equitable basis for new or expanded public improvements needed to support the

Circulation Element
C 2.4:
Transportation Fee Ordinance. Require new developments to pay their 
proportionate share of the costs for planned on and off site roadway 
improvements. Utilize a Transportation Fee Ordinance to finance necessary 
improvement equitably. 
C 2.5:
Traffic Studies.  Require site-specific traffic studies for development projects 
where there may be a substantial impact on the local street system.  Traffic 
impacts caused by a development project are considered to be unacceptable and 
warrant mitigation if the addition of project traffic results in a cumulative 
intersection level of service exceeding the acceptable level established in Policy C-
2.1; where there may be safety hazards created; or where there may be other 
substantial impacts on the circulation system. 
C 2.10: 
Transportation Demand Management (TDM).  Participate in the TDM Program as 
outlined by the San Mateo City/County Association of Governments (C/CAG).  
Encourage TDM measures as a condition of approval for development projects, 
which are anticipated to cause substantial traffic impacts. C/CAG requires the 
preparation of a TDM program for all new development that would add 100 peak 
hour trips or more to the regional road network.
C 2.12: 
Transportation Demand Management (TDM) in Downtown. Establish and 
implement a TDM program, a Transportation Management Association (TMA), 
and other measures to reduce vehicle trips and encourage transit use and 
promote bicycle and pedestrian accessibility for development within one-half mile 
of the Downtown transit center.
C 4.1:
Bicycle Master Plan.  Implement the Bicycle Master Plan’s recommended 
programs and projects to create and maintain a fully-connected safe and logical 
bikeways system; support the City's Sustainable Transportation Actions; and 
coordinate with the countywide system.

UD 2.1:        Multi-Family Design. Ensure that new multi-family developments substantially 
conform to the City’s Multi-family and Small Lot Multi-Family Design Guidelines 
that address the preservation and enhancement of neighborhood character 
through building scale, materials, architectural style, quality of construction, open 
space, location of parking and lot size.
UD 2.2:        Building Scale. Ensure that new multi-family developments respect the existing 
scale of the neighboring buildings by providing a change in the building face at 
spacings common to existing buildings and by stepping down building height 
towards the street to more closely match the height of existing buildings.
UD2.3:
Style and Materials. Encourage the design of new multi-family developments in 
areas with a dominant building style or dominant type of exterior building 
materials to complement the style and incorporate the common materials of the 
area.
UD 2.4:
Multi Family Parking. Encourage new multi-family developments to place parking 
underground or towards the rear of the parcel to avoid blank, ground floor walls 
and to screen views of parking from the street.
UD 2.5:
Multi-Family Open Space. Require that a portion of required open space be 
useable for passive or active recreation.
UD 2.6:
Orient Buildings Toward the Street.  Encourage commercial development to be 
located at the street in retail areas to encourage pedestrian activity and the use 
of on-street parking.  Locate required parking towards the side and rear of 
parcels.
UD 2.7:
Respect Existing Scale. Encourage new commercial development to respect the 
scale of surrounding buildings by providing breaks in the building face at spacings 
common to buildings in the area and by stepping back upper floors.
UD 2.9:
Pedestrian Oriented Design.  On retail commercial projects, designate pedestrian 
activity as a priority through the design and provision of adequate sidewalk 
widths, locating windows along ground floor street facades, trees and awnings, 
and human scale construction materials and features.
UD 2.14: 
Sustainable Design and Building Construction. Require new development and 
building alterations to conform with the City's Sustainable Initiatives Plan and

Noise Element
N 1.1:
Interior Noise Level Standard. Require submittal of an acoustical analysis and 
interior noise insulation for all “noise sensitive” land uses listed in Table N-1 that 
have an exterior noise level of 60 dB (Ldn) or above, as shown on Figure N-1. The 
maximum interior noise level shall not exceed 45 dB (Ldn) in any habitable rooms.
N 1.2:
Exterior Noise Level Standard. Require submittal of an acoustical analysis for new 
parks, play areas, and multi-family common open space (intended for the use and 
the enjoyment of residents) that have an exterior noise level of 60dB (Ldn) or above, 
as shown on Figure N-1. Require an acoustical analysis that uses peak hour Leq for 
new parks and play areas. Require a feasibility analysis of noise reduction measures 
for public parks and play areas. Incorporate necessary mitigation measures into 
residential project design to minimize common open space noise levels. Maximum 
exterior noise should not exceed 67 dB (Ldn) for residential land uses and should 
not exceed 65 dB (Leq) during the noisiest hour for public park uses. 
N 2.1: 
Noise Ordinance. Continue implementation and enforcement of the City's existing 
noise control ordinance: a) which prohibits noise that is annoying or injurious to 
neighbors of normal sensitivity, making such activity a public nuisance, and b) 
restricts the hours of construction to minimize noise impact.

General Plan Elements and Policies
PA-2023-025, 668 E. 3rd Ave., Post + Beam Pre-Application
Page 8 of 8
N 2.2:
Minimize Noise Impact.  Protect all “noise-sensitive” land uses listed in Tables N-1 
and N-2 from adverse impacts caused by the noise generated on-site by new 
developments. Incorporate necessary mitigation measures into development 
design to minimize noise impacts. Prohibit long-term exposure increases of 3dB 
(Ldn) or greater at the common property line, or new uses which generate noise 
levels of 60 dB (Ldn) or greater at the property line, excluding existing ambient noise 
levels. 
N 2.3:         
Minimize Commercial Noise.  Protect land uses other than those listed as "noise 
sensitive" in Table N 1 from adverse impacts caused by the on-site noise generated 
by new developments.  Incorporate necessary mitigation measures into 
development design to minimize noise impacts.  Prohibit new uses which generate 
noise levels of 65 dB (LDN) or above at the property line, excluding ambient noise 
levels.

April 20, 2023 
 
Ms. Linda Ly

Re: 
Request for Density Bonus Consistent with Government Code Section 65915 
for Proposed Project Located at 668 3rd Avenue and 316 Eldorado Street 
 
Dear Ms. Ly: 
 
On behalf of Gateway Crossing SM, LLC (“Applicant”), this letter serves as a 
request for a density bonus, waivers, and a concession consistent with State Density Bonus Law 
(Gov. Code § 65915) for the proposed mixed-use development, consisting of 59 residential units 
and a 131,635 square-foot office building (“Project”), located at 668 3rd Avenue and 316 
Eldorado Street (APNs 034-188-140 and -150) (“Property”) in the City of San Mateo (“City”). 
 
The Project proposes a total of 59 residential units, with 15 percent of the 49 
base units, or 7.35 lower income units restricted to lower income households (80% Area 
Median Income (AMI) or less) required to comply with the City’s Below Market Rate 
(Inclusionary) Program. The Project would provide 7 lower-income units onsite (the 
“Affordable Units”), representing 14% of the base project, and fee out for the partial 0.35 units. 
The Property is located within ½ mile of at least one major transit stop. The Affordable Units 
and the Project location therefore qualify the Project for a twenty-six percent (26%) density 
bonus and one concession. (Gov. Code §§ 65915(d)(2)(A); 65915(f)(1).) Because the project is 
located within a 1/2 mile of a major transit stop, under Government Code Section 65863.2 (AB 
2097), there is no minimum parking requirement for either the residential or commercial 
component of the project.  
 
Government Code Section 65915(f)(1)— Requested Density Bonus 
 
By providing 14% of the Project as on-site affordable units, the Project qualifies 
for a twenty-six percent (26%) density bonus which would permit up to 62 units. (Gov’t Code § 
65915(f)(1).) The Project site is 0.98 acres and its CBD/S zoning district permits 50 units per 
acre. Thus, the base project would be 49 units. The Project requests a twenty percent (20%) 
density bonus for a total of up to 59 residential units. 
 
Government Code Section 65915(e)(1)— Requested Waivers of Development Standards 
 
Government Code Section 65915(e)(1) provides, in part, that “in no case may a 
city, county, or city and county apply any development standard that will have the effect of

--- page 87 ---
Page 2 
 
 
physically precluding the construction of a [density bonus project] at the densities or with the 
concessions or incentives permitted by this section.” The right to waivers has been broadly 
interpreted by the courts. (Wollmer v. City of Berkeley (2011) 193 Cal.App.4th 1329, 1346– 
1347.) 
 
The Applicant is requesting waivers from the following development standards 
that physically preclude the development of the proposed density bonus project: 
 
▪ Floor Area Ratio (FAR) (Zoning Code § 27.62.160). The proposed 
density bonus project requires a FAR of 4.50 which exceeds the otherwise 
applicable FAR of 3.0. Application of the 3.0 FAR limitation would result 
in the loss of affordable housing units and the commercial square footage 
intended to help subsidize the affordable housing units. The increase in 
FAR is very similar to the FAR increase granted for the 400 E. 5th 
Avenue and 480 E. 4th Avenue project, where additional FAR was needed 
to accommodate affordable housing units and a public parking garage. The 
additional FAR is necessary to prevent the physical preclusion of the 
density bonus project. 
 
▪ Residential Height. The seven-story residential structure would have a top 
of upper roof of approximately 75’.  The roof plate of the elevator overrun 
and stair tower roof access would be 83’- 6”. This exceeds the Property’s 
height limit of 55’.  The Project requires a minimum of 28’- 6” of 
additional height to not be physically precluded and may require 
additional height as the Project design is refined during processing. 
 
▪ Residential Open Space (Zoning Code § 27.38.130).  The City requires 80 
square feet of private usable open space per unit, or common usable open 
space of 150% of the private requirement. The Project is able to provide 
approximately 2,940 square feet of common usable open space through a 
courtyard, terrace, and a top floor amenity deck, which does not meet 
7,080 square feet of common usable open space required for the Project. 
The Project is also providing 1,512 square feet of private open space 
through 27 balconies.  However, these balconies do not meet minimum 
dimension requirements.  Increasing the size of the courtyard, terrace, 
balconies, or amenity deck would require a reduction in residential 
building mass which in turn would require the loss of residential units. 
The rooftop area cannot be utilized as a roof deck based on the project’s 
highest occupiable floor allowance.  Thus, a waiver is required from the 
residential open space requirements so that the Project is not physically 
precluded. 
 
Government Code Section 65915(d)— Requested Concession 
 
A concession or incentive is a “reduction in site development standards or a 
modification of zoning code requirements or architectural design requirements . . . or other 
regulatory incentives or concessions proposed by the developer . . . that result in identifiable and

--- page 88 ---
Page 3 
 
 
actual cost reductions to provide for affordable housing costs.” (Gov. Code § 65915(k)(3).) A 
city “shall grant the concession or incentive requested by the applicant unless the city . . . makes 
a written finding, based upon substantial evidence, of any of the following: 
 
(A) The concession or incentive does not result in identifiable and actual cost 
reductions, [], to provide for affordable housing costs . . . . 
 
(B) The concession or incentive would have a specific, adverse impact . . . upon 
public health and safety or the physical environment or on any real property that is listed 
in the California Register of Historical Resources . . . . 
 
(C) The concession or incentive would be contrary to state or federal law.” 
 
(Gov. Code § 65915(d)(1).) Since 2017, the Density Bonus Law no longer requires a showing 
that a requested concession is required to make a project economically feasible. (Stats. 2016, ch. 
758, § 1.) 
 
The Project qualifies for one (1) concession under Density Bonus Law. The Applicant requests the 
following one concession: 
 
▪ Commercial Height. The six-story commercial structure would have a top 
of upper roof of approximately 88’. The roof plate of the mechanical 
penthouse would be 102’- 0”. This exceeds the Property’s height limit of 
55’. The additional 48’- 0” of height would permit two additional stories 
of commercial uses. The revenue generated by the additional square 
footage permitted by this concession would subsidize the Project’s 
affordable housing costs and would be in scale with the Project’s 
residential structure.  
 
The Applicant may amend this Density Bonus request as the Project is refined through 
processing. Please feel free to call me if you have any questions and we look forward to working 
with you on this exciting project. 
 
 
Yours Sincerely, 
 
Preston O’Connell 
Partner 
Harvest Properties, Inc.

Information Required for Planning Commission Study Session 
 
___________      1. 
For the Written Project Description, please clarify whether the proposed 
“Commercial Office” use include any retail. 
___________      2. 
For the Density Bonus & BMR Unit Information Request Form, please review 
and revise the redline corrections. Additionally, the City requires documentation 
that there will be a “cost reduction” as a result of the requested concessions in 
order to make the required finding that the request results in a cost reduction 
to provide for affordable housing costs (see Government Code Section 
65915(d)(1)). Based on the Density Bonus request letter included in the initial

a. Please elaborate on the cost reductions resulting from the Concession and 
confirm that the cost reductions are less than the cost of constructing the 
affordable units. 
b. Please review and confirm any changes or additional waivers/concessions 
due to the comments contained in this comment letter. 
___________      3. 
Please include a floor area diagram or table for each floor, in consideration of 
the following: 
a. Note that floor area is measured to the exterior wall surfaces and to the 
mid-point of shared walls. 
b. Multi-level areas including the stairs and elevator footprints shall be 
counted once at the ground level in the total floor area. 
c. Stories exceeding 15 ft. in height shall be counted as additional floor area. 
The residential building shows a lounge on Floor 7 that has an interior 
ceiling height of 19 ft. and shall be counted twice in floor area. 
d. Bicycle parking facilities are excluded from floor area calculations. Please 
see SMMC 27.04.020(b)(2) for a full list of exclusions. Please calculate these 
areas separately. 
e. If “Commercial Office” includes any retail, then provide an estimated 
breakdown between the different retail and office areas.

project information table. 
Code and Policy Concerns 
___________      5. 
The General Plan’s Urban Design Element encourages large-scale, mixed-use 
developments to provide a transition and respect existing neighborhood scale. 
Staff recommends refining the building mass by providing additional stepbacks 
and pedestrian scale improvements as the project approaches the R5-D zone 
and lower height buildings directly northeast of the project site. Please see 
Urban Design Policy UD 2.2 and UD 2.7 for additional guidance. 
___________      6. 
This project is located in the Gateway subarea and is subject to the Vision of the 
Gateway design guidelines. Please be advised of the following requirements: 
a. E. 3rd Avenue is a “boulevard” and requires a 15 ft. to 20 ft. setback along 
the street frontage. For portions of the building above 30 ft. in height, 
please provide an additional 8 ft. stepback minimum. See diagram below. 
b. S. Eldorado St. is a “neighborhood street,” which requires additional 
setbacks of 15 ft. to 20 ft. For portions of the building over 25 ft. in height, 
please provide an additional stepback of 8 ft. minimum. 
c. Front porches and stoop entrances are allowed to encroach within the 
neighborhood street setback area. See diagram below. 
 
 
___________      7. 
The City’s BMR Program requires Below Market Rate (BMR) units to be 
distributed throughout the development. See BMR Guidelines, VII. Unit Size, 
Type and Design. Additional comments to follow once detailed floor plans are 
provided during the Formal Planning Application. 
 
___________      8. 
Update all building elevations and sections to measure building height from 
existing grade and not finished floor or slab. Measure to top of building plate 
line and roof peak or parapet walls.

an improved transition to lower scale buildings north and east of the site 
through changes in building massing and stepbacks. Additional setbacks should 
be provided along S. Eldorado St. to ensure a consistent building rhythm and 
improved pedestrian environment that respects the existing neighborhood 
context and adjacent buildings (Metropolitan). 
___________      3. 
Staff recommends refinement of the building facades through changes in 
material, window proportions, color, and other methods for increased visual 
interest. The current repetition of windows throughout the buildings creates a 
lack of focal point. The residential building façade would benefit from having a 
more defined building base, body and top to break up the vertical massing. This

--- page 93 ---
Page 5 of 17 
 
can be achieved through subtle changes in colors and materials. The commercial 
building at the intersection of E. 3rd Avenue and S. Delaware Street should 
consider changes in building colors and materials especially at the building base. 
This will also allow the project to meet the Vision of the Gateway and 
Downtown Area Plan design goals, which encourages pedestrian scale design 
and site elements that create a positive transition from the Gateway to the 
Downtown core. 
___________      4. 
Due to the high visibility this project will have for visitors entering San Mateo 
from 3rd Ave, the project should consider further refinements to the building 
corner at 3rd Ave on S. Eldorado St. Consider special architectural details that 
create a positive, balanced focal point for the building. Staff recommends 
refining these building corners through integration of additional open space, 
stepbacks, articulation, etc. Consider corner treatments throughout the building 
to provide variation and architectural interest. 
___________      5. 
Usable open space and site landscaping is intended to compliment new multi-
family developments and support the enjoyment of residents on-site. Please 
consider increasing usable open space and amenities throughout the residential 
building, as well as overall site landscaping to be more consistent with other 
multifamily developments in the Gateway corridor.

may not pass over any vertical features that are tall enough to result in 
a collision.  Wheel tracks and overhangs may not pass over any on-
street parking areas or loading zones. 
B. 
Wheel tracks and overhangs of SU-30 vehicles turning from Street A to 
Street B may not cross into oncoming traffic on Street B if the opposing 
direction of traffic on Street B is uncontrolled or controlled by a traffic 
signal.

Formal Planning Application Comments 
 
___________      1. 
TREE PROTECTION MEASURES - This project is subject to San Mateo Municipal 
Code 13.40, and 27.71 please submit an Arborist Report and Tree Protection 
Plan (TPP) for revision. A TPP is required whenever any Construction Activity is 
to be performed within a radius measured from the trunk equal to 10 times the 
diameter of the tree trunk measured at 54" above grade for any Protected 
Tree*(s). This includes trees on the subject property, neighboring properties, or, 
in the public right-of-way. The TPP shall be prepared by an ISA Certified Arborist 
(Project Arborist) who provides consulting services and is familiar with the 
Municipal Code and the industry best practices. The requirements for a TPP can

--- page 101 ---
Page 13 of 17 
 
be found on the PROTECTED TREES ORDINANCE ADMINISTRATIVE GUIDELINES 
section Tree Protection Specifications.    
___________      2. 
TREE EVALUATION SCHEDULE - Submit an Evaluation/Appraisal of all existing 
trees over 6 inches in caliper. The tree species, condition, and location values of 
the trees shall be based on an evaluation by an experienced landscape appraiser 
recognized by the American Society of Consulting Arborists utilizing the most 
recent Guide for Plant Appraisal, in compliance with SMMC 27.71.150. Provide 
an excel spreadsheet to record individual tree attributes like Tag number, 
common name, botanical name, trunk diameter, protected status, overall 
condition, possible impacts from construction operations, and its project status 
(preserve, remove, relocate). Please note that Street trees and on-site trees 
shall be evaluated differently per the updated chapter 27.71. 
 
___________      3. 
REQUIRED TREE PLANTING FORM - Provide the Required Tree Planting form that 
includes the LU value of trees to be removed or preserved and also 
Replacement Trees if applicable. Specify the in-lieu fees to be paid to the city. 
The Required Tree Planting form can be found on page 31 of the Planning 
Application Guide. 
 
___________      4. 
TREE PROTECTION PLAN SHEET - Provide a full-size scaled site plan showing the 
location of all Protected trees with accurate driplines in relation to the proposed 
work. Number the trees as per the Arborist report and, show the location of 
tree protection measures specified in the Tree Protection Plan, including but not 
limited to fencing, trunk wrap, soil protection, areas of excavation by hand, air, 
or water. The plan set shall reference the sheet number(s) where the Tree 
Protection Plan and Tree Protection Plan Sheet can be found. 
 
___________      5. 
ARBORIST REPORT IS PART OF THE PLAN - The Arborist Report shall be 
reproduced on one or more full-size sheets and included in the Plan Set properly 
indexed. Make sure the report is still readable and important details will not be 
missed.    
___________      6. 
SITE PLAN UPDATE -The Overall Site plan must be updated to show the accurate 
tree dripline and the location of protection measures as specified by the 
Arborist's tree protection plan. 
 
___________      7. 
INFORMATIONAL - Protected trees for this project are as follows: any trees over 
6 inches in diameter on the subject property (as per SMMC 27.71), Heritage 
Trees only on neighboring properties (as per section 13.40), and Street Trees of 
any size in the public right-of-way within 30 feet of the project (as per section 
13.40).

Parks and Recreation: 
 
___________      1. 
This project is subject to the Park In-Lieu/Impact Fee (SMMC 26.64.010 & 
13.05.070). Based on the City Council approval of the fees for Fiscal Year 
2022/23 which took effect on July 1, 2022, the fee per dwelling unit (which is 
valid until June 30, 2023) for projects of this type (Multi-family 5+ units) is

--- page 102 ---
Page 14 of 17 
 
$20,476.00 per unit.  From this set of plans, this project will have a net increase 
of 59 Multi Family 5+ units. Therefore, based on Fiscal Year 2022/23 fee 
information the total current fee for the project is calculated to be 
$1,208,084.00 (which is valid until June 30, 2022). This fee is subject to change 
each fiscal year starting July 1st based on an updated fee per unit included in 
the City’s Comprehensive Fee Schedule for the Fiscal Year the payment is made. 
The fee is due prior to the issuance of the first building permit. Just prior to the 
time of payment, contact the Department of Parks and Recreation to obtain the 
actual amount of the fee due. Please note that the Building Department 
typically calculates a Park and Recreation Tax for your project. However, you are 
only required to pay the greater amount between the Park In-Lieu / Impact Fee 
and the Park and Recreation Tax. The Park In-Lieu fee is typically greater than 
the Park and Recreation Tax so in that case no Park and Recreation Tax should 
be charged if the Park In-Lieu Fee is paid first. 
___________      2. 
In reviewing the plan set submitted for the initial pre-application review in April 
2023, sheets LR 1.0, LR1.1 and AR2.04 include seating areas and a lounge.  The 
lounge is less that 1000 sf in size which is the minimum size to be considered for 
park and recreation facility space credit, so it does not qualify for credit.  
Therefore, the project only includes 1 facility type (outdoor seating area) for 
credit.   Based on the residential unit count of 59 units, per Section SMMC 
26.64.030 (b) (8) (A) at least two park and recreation facility space credit types 
must be provided in order to meet the minimum threshold to receive credit.  
Therefore, no credits can be given. Attached is the Private Park and Recreation 
Space Credit Listing which describes parameters for the various types of park 
and recreation facilities in order to qualify for credit.

space.   
2.  Must be provided with night lighting evening play up to 10 pm 
with provisions for maximum light cut off and glare protection 
onto adjacent units based on approved information. 
Dog Park /Run Area 
1300 SF and a 
minimum width of 
15’. 
Applicable only to developments which allow dogs.     Maximum 
size shall not exceed 10% of the total parkland dedication 
requirement size of dog runs or minimum size, whichever is 
greater.  For projects less than 50 units, the credit shall be reduced 
by the amount of proposed units / 50 units.   Dog run / park areas 
shall: 
1.  Have a 4’ high perimeter fence and be gated.  
2.  Not be located on slopes greater than 4:1.   
3.  Be free from drainage from outside areas.     
4.  Have a surface such as decomposed granite or as approved by 
the City. 
5.  Be provided with sitting area for dog owners to sit and dogs to 
rest that is protected from the shade via trees or shade structure. 
 6. Include trash and recycling receptacles, drinking fountain for 
humans and dogs, pet bag dispenser and signage with rules. 
Outdoor Eating 
Area 
Projects 5 units or 
less: 230 SF. 
Projects greater 
than 5 units:  50% 
of maximum 
allowable SF limit 
based on unit count 
or 230 sf whichever 
is greater. 
Maximum credit shall be limited to 4 SF x the total quantity of 
residential units or the required minimum size whichever is 
greater. The area be designed to meet the following parameters: 
1. Shall consist of eating tables and seating, grilling area of at least 
1 square foot plus 1 sf per 10 eating table seats, trash and recycling 
containers and potable water for each area.  If grilling area 
requires coals a coal bin shall be provided for each area. All 
features must be fixed in place.  
2.  Tables shall be within 50’ of grilling area & not separated by 
gates and at least 50% of the eating tables and shall be designed to 
include provisions for sun protection (trees, other approved shade 
elements) for at least 3 hours during the hours between 11 am and 
5 pm during summer solstice.   
3.   Area to be counted for credit shall consist of area which eating 
tables including seats, grills, potable water and trash/recycling 
features occupy plus the needed pedestrian circulation area to 
access such features (within 2’ of such features) within the space 
excluding adjacent pedestrian circulation space (i.e adjacent 
pathways).   
Outdoor seating 
areas 
23 SF 
Maximum credit shall be limited to 7 SF per the total quantity of 
residential units.  Excludes seating areas that are included in other 
facility type areas being given credit and elements within seating 
area that are not fixed in place. At least 50% of that space must 
protected from the sun between 11am and 3pm.  
 
The area to be counted shall: 
1.  Include seating areas such as benches located along pathways 
within landscaped areas and areas that contain picnic tables that 
do not qualify for outdoor eating areas.   
2.  Include trash / recycling containers if picnic tables are provided.  
3.  Consist of the area which benches, picnic tables, trash/recycling 
containers and other approved features occupy the space plus the 
needed pedestrian circulation area to access such features (within

POST + BEAM NEIGHBORHOOD MEETING NOTES 
Monday, June 26, 2023, 7:00 PM – 8:00 PM 
 
Public Attendees (~20 total): David Light, Bob, George, Arion Paylo, NC, Lindy Hewitt, Laurie, BC, Olya, Brian 
Shields, Amy, Mia, Binh 
Applicant Attendees: Preston O’Connell, Kevin Choy, Jonathan Stone, Don Peterson, Eddie Piatt, Kylo Filomeo, 
Chris Jew 
City Staff Attendees: Julia Klein, Linda Ly 
• David Light:  
o Topic: Parking 
o Comment: Curious whether cars will be utilized just for residents or also commercial office 
users. Currently lives on Fremont Street – concerned about greater traffic loads on Fremont. 
o Preston: We’re still early on and haven’t quite figured out all the mechanics. We will be 
developing a traffic demand management plan and completing a traffic analysis to better 
understand what impacts, if any, will need to be mitigated. 
• Bob:  
o Topic: Neighborhood Retail 
o Comment: Lives a couple blocks from the site and is concerned about groceries, 7-11 is where 
he shops, and also goes to Draeger’s. Doesn’t drive and takes public transportation. 
o Preston: We will evaluate the potential inclusion of retail. 
• George:  
o Topic: Neighborhood Retail 
o Comment: Complete disregard for the neighborhood by eliminating local neighborhood retail. 
Coordinate with Samtrans to put a bus stop in front of the building. 
o Preston: We will evaluate the potential inclusion of Retail and a potential bus stop shift. 
• Arion Paylo:  
o Topic: Neighborhood Retail 
o Comment: Concerned about losing the affordable, great-quality restaurant. Plans that were 
submitted didn’t mention retail, but the presentation did mention retail. On the El Dorado side, 
the reality is that the unemployed laborers loiter in the area. Losing family-owned restaurants is 
a large issue. There is currently no crosswalk to access the parking at Metropolitan. 
o Response (Preston): There is no retail on this project. Right now, it seems like there is a lot of 
retail vacancy, so there will be an analysis of where retail will be most effective. 
o Response (Kevin): The project will include a proposal for a mid-block crossing to access the 
Metropolitan apartments parking.  
• NC:  
o Topic: Building architecture and design 
o Comment: What is the building height?  Given the building is 6 stories high.  Would that exceed 
the building exceeds the height limit and surrounding buildings? 
o Response (Kevin): Residential: 75 ft height, Commercial 85 ft height. 
o Response (Preston): It is an attempt to max out the residency for market rate and affordable 
housing units.

--- page 107 ---
2 
o Response (Linda): There is a building height limitation of 55ft. Their application is still 
preliminary and is under review. 
• NC:  
o Topic: Parking 
o Comment: This question is for Linda Ly and the city planning - With the speed and number of 
developments in this 'Gateway' neighborhood, does the city have any plan to install city parking 
structures like in Downtown area? 
o Julia: The City has installed the new 5th garage east of the railroad tracks. No additional parking 
structures are planned. 
• Lindy Hewitt:  
o Topic: Building design and architecture 
o Comment: Generally disturbed by all the city blocks being leveled, changing the character of the 
city drastically. With the new height it is 50% higher than current. Transforming the city into not 
a pretty city in my opinion. 
o Preston: Thank you for the comments. 
• Laurie:  
o Topic: Architecture and Traffic 
o Comment: The project should utilize architecture that blends in better – potentially 
contemporary Mediterranean. A traffic study needs to be completed. There are larger moving 
vans that need to be accommodated in the project so that another lane is not blocked. Amazon, 
UPS, Uber, may there needs to be a temporary parking zone. The lighting impacts at night for 
the residents that live in the surrounding area, they had to install drapes to block out more 
light. 
o Preston: Thank you for the comments. We will include a lighting study as part of the 
entitlement process.   
• BC: The city seems to be turning the city into Syria or Turkey (high density). Can the city complete due 
diligence to justify the safety of neighbors? Can it show that the ground is stable enough to hold the 
tall building? 
o Linda: The city building division requires technical studies to make sure that the applicant’s 
plans are up to the building code. 
• Olya:  
o Topic: Building height, neighborhood retail, acquire gas station 
o Comment: Please respect Measure Y. Include neighborhood retail within the project plan and 
acquire the gas station as part of the project. 
o Preston: Thank you for the comments. We had conversations with the owner of the gas station 
and they were not interested in selling. We cannot force a private entity to sell their property. 
• Brian Shields - Nor Cal Carpenters Union 
o Topic: Construction 
o Comment: Thank you for building mass timber. The carpenter’s union has a certification to 
install the mass timber and use the appropriate rigging to install. Thank you. 
• Amy, Mia, Binh 
o Topic: Building height, neighborhood retail, traffic, and amount of projects 
o Comment: Real concerns about traffic studies. Right now, during rush hour it is backed up on 
3rd and 4th going in and out of the downtown area. This is a very working-class immigrant 
neighborhood, and they keep losing retail and eating options that the residents can afford and 
it’s leading to food trucks all over the neighborhood that increases litter all over the area. 
o Preston: Thank you for your comment.

From: Keith Weber

Mr. O'Connell, 
On September 1st of last year you wrote me a very nice email in response to my comment letter on PA-2022-023, 
adjacent to the Downtown Historic District.  My letter stated that the project was an "opportunity to create a distinctive 
architectural statement that will compliment some of downtown's more outstanding buildings."  I also requested that 
"you consider a more traditional design style of architecture for the project."  I included photos of successful examples 
from other communities. 
 
You wrote back and said, "Your letter clearly articulates the importance of respecting the Downtown area’s historic fabric 
while creating a unique architectural statement that will tie into the established neighborhood context."  You went on to 
say, "We agree with you. It is our top design priority to create an architecture that mediates between the historic 
vernacular and contemporary demands for the interior space." 
 
Although not directly abutting the Historic District like 401-445 Sl B St., the Post + Beam project is near the Historic 
District and does exert an influence.  Once again, I respectfully request that you consider a design that is more 
compatible with the traditional - and architecturally diverse - character of downtown.  
 
I include two example projects located in San Mateo that I would say successfully mediate between compatible historic 
style and contemporary demands for interior space.    I compare these newer projects with two downtown historic 
buildings with similar style and design elements. 
Thank you for your consideration. 
Keith Weber

further away, approximately a 1/3 of a mile, and believe there is a design aesthetic that balances the modern and the
historic. We would appreciate if we could meet with you over a coffee to discuss your comments in greater detail. Let us

668 E. Third Avenue project
 My first comment is for the developer.  Why would you want to build, soon to be empty, office space?  There’s already 
abundant empty office space in nearby San Francisco.  Downtown SF has 18.4 million sf of empty office space. Secondly, 
people are beginning and continuing to work from home. Additionally, it is a well-known fact that numerous firms are 
leaving Silicon Valley for Texas, Nevada, and other less highly taxed states. 
 
Who in their right mind would want to move to a complex that has such inadequate parking facilities?  Why would 
anybody move to a complex that has no visitor parking space? 
 
Why would the planning commission approve this eyesore? Have you considered our infrastructure? Once again, have 
you considered D increase traffic in an already overcrowded downtown area?   
 
I find this tendency to overbuild to be a slap in the face to current residents.  
 
I look forward to voting for officials who will limit unsustainable “growth”.

Jerry, 
First of all, thank you for your comments on our project. The team at Harvest prioriƟzes our engagement with the 
surrounding community across all of our projects and will take into account the comments we receive to ensure the 
project responds to and respects the local environment.  
Regarding your ﬁrst comment about commercial oﬃce, we agree that there is a vacancy issue in San Francisco’s 
commercial oﬃce, but we also see a strong ﬂight to quality oﬃce space that is well-located, near transit, and well-
ameniƟzed. A great example of this is the 300,000 square feet of oﬃce space under construcƟon in San Mateo – 
approximately 90% of this space is leased. AddiƟonally, our team is parƟcularly aware of the jobs/housing imbalance 
across the Bay Area and reﬂect that in proposing oﬃce development in appropriate locaƟons; the upcoming San Mateo 
General Plan designates Oﬃce in the downtown area. In fact, the Harvest team recently proposed, received 
enƟtlements, and began construcƟon of our project, Peninsula Heights, which eliminated 225,000 square feet of 
commercial oﬃce and replaced it with 290 for-sale homes. We believe that commercial developments close to the 
downtown are of criƟcal importance to enlivening the downtown core by providing a dayƟme populaƟon to the 
downtown retailers. This parƟcular project, which is approximately a third of a mile from Caltrain and Downtown is the 
perfect place to construct a commercial and residenƟal development. Last but not least, we are excited to not only 
provide commercial oﬃce, but also residenƟal units within this project; the 59 units would not be possible without 
uƟlizing the commercial oﬃces residenƟal unit allocaƟon in addiƟon to a bonus provided by State Density Law. 
Regarding parking, we couldn’t agree more that providing adequate parking for both residenƟal and commercial is of 
vital importance. For this project, we are proposing to uƟlize approximately 60 parking stalls in Metropolitan, the 
apartment across the street, to support the residenƟal project which equate to a parking raƟo of one to one.  
Regarding your comments on design, our team was thoughƞul in our approach to the design and worked to set the 
building back at upper levels to align what will be perceived as the top of building to match the other structures along 3rd
Avenue. We are providing extensive sidewalk improvements, widening the sidewalk along 3rd avenue from 8’ – 12’ to 22’ 
– 36’ and incorporaƟng mature trees and vibrant landscaping for use by the public. That said, we understand this if the
ﬁrst Ɵme the Public and the City is seeing this project and expect further design iteraƟon to blend our projects design 
into the adjacent vernacular. 
Again, we greatly appreciate your thoughts regarding our project and are happy to listen and conƟnue the dialogue. Let 
us know if you would like to setup a Ɵme for us to meet to discuss further. 
P.S. – I do have the Planning Commissioners on BCC in this email for transparency. 
Thanks, 
Kevin Choy, P.E. | Associate Director 
Harvest Properties, Inc.

From:

Thursday, May 11, 2023 11:15 AM

Subject:
Comments on Post & Beam - PA - 2023-025
Good morning - 
I am a resident of Central San Mateo and have the following comments to be considered for the Post & Beam project 
submission: 
- Why are we considering building more office space, when we have been mandated by the state to build housing?  My 
assumption is that it must be cheaper and more profitable to build office space. We already have over 856,000 sf of new 
office space in downtown San Mateo. Look at the problem San Francisco is facing with 18.4 million sf of empty office 
space.  I ask you, who have the power to make these decisions, to please concentrate on our housing needs! 
- Some say that Measure Y constrains our ability to build housing, but consider that we are allocated a full 2 stories of 
free state density bonus which doesn’t count against our RHNA numbers 
- Parking for residents (8 spaces for 69 units) in the proposed building is inadequate.  Workers in the building would be 
more likely able to commute to this building, but residents will need a car to access schools, grocery stores, potential 
work, medical appointments and other errands.  Unfortunately our public transportation is not adequate for managing 
daily living activities. Consider providing guest parking for residents as well. Inadequate parking in these new buildings 
impact the neighborhood streets, as I see people parking in our neighborhood every day and walking to new building 
sites on Claremont 
- The project architecture needs to blend in better with our existing neighborhood. Choose a less “boxy” style and 
ensure there are tall trees and landscaping to maintain some greenery near our neighbhorhoods  
Thank you for your attention. 
Frances Souza

Subject: Construction in Downtown San Mateo 
 
Dear City Council, Mr. Bustos, and Ms. Olds, 
San Mateo used to be a wonderful, family-friendly place to live with amenities nearby. We had all the elements: a quaint 
downtown, amazing views of the hills and bay, a smaller more connected community, beautiful old architecture, etc. 
This should be the perfect time and opportunity to keep and enhance what makes San Mateo a truly special and unique 
place to live. However, I am exceedingly frustrated and saddened by what has been happening over the past several 
years. The City of San Mateo is being destroyed faster than I ever imagined was possible. 
Against the residents wishes and concerns, the City Council keeps approving and shoving more huge developments 
down the pipeline. Our precious city is being overrun by greedy developers building the most ugly, generic, blocky, 
cheap looking, monstrosities which go right up to the sidewalk with no greenery. The downtown area is getting 
crowded, claustrophobic, looks unattractive, and gets worse with each new development. The once beautiful views are 
starting to get blocked off by tall buildings. Don't make it worse by repealing Measure Y. Residents need to be able to 
stay connected to the nature around them. It's an important part of why people live here. It is beneficial and 
necessary  for our health and well-being. 
It is clear that the city does not need any more office space, as there are lots of vacancies. I don't understand why the 
city is tearing down block after block, and jamming in more and more people, when our infrastructure is failing and can't 
even support the current community. The roads and sidewalks are in complete disrepair; it's honestly an

--- page 122 ---
2
embarrassment. Traffic has gotten so bad that it's near impossible to get across town, especially during commute hours. 
That will only continue to get worse with all the new construction going on and potential future projects. 
The city needs to stop construction projects like Block 20 and 21 so these issues can be addressed and fixed. Demolition 
permits should be tied directly to building permits, so we don't end up with an eyesore of empty lots with dirt mounds 
and tree stumps for years to come. The city should be focusing on quality of life issues and environmental stewardship. 
Buildings should be built farther back from the sidewalk to allow for landscaping and mature trees to provide shade for 
pedestrians. We should incorporate new green methods, taking advantage of vertical space to have living walls, have 
underground parking garages with a park on top, etc. 
The City Council needs to push back against the developers, construction companies, and the state to take our city back. 
Don't let them cheat us out of the future of our home. They need to be respectful and responsive to residents and 
contribute to our community. If there are delays, they should make that up to the residents by investing in our 
downtown. Listen to the residents who voted you in and follow their lead. We need to support small businesses, have a 
wide variety of services, and more green space. We are calling for action. Please restore the heart and soul of San 
Mateo. 
Sincerely, 
Erin White
